      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2686333726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9616047210300923390">I am Jack's disappointing sequel. <br/><br/>Chuck Palahniuk follows up his Fight Club novel (slightly different than the movie) with a comic series collected here. Our protagonist (here named Sebastian) is 10 years older, married to Marla Singer and father to a precocious little child. He's popping pills and living in a haze, doing whatever employed, middle aged white guys do in these sorts of stories.<br/><br/>It's Fight Club. But older! It's the movie except everyone knows the twist about Brad Pitt and Ed Norton </span>
  <span id="freeText9616047210300923390" style="display:none">I am Jack's disappointing sequel. <br /><br />Chuck Palahniuk follows up his Fight Club novel (slightly different than the movie) with a comic series collected here. Our protagonist (here named Sebastian) is 10 years older, married to Marla Singer and father to a precocious little child. He's popping pills and living in a haze, doing whatever employed, middle aged white guys do in these sorts of stories.<br /><br />It's Fight Club. But older! It's the movie except everyone knows the twist about Brad Pitt and Ed Norton before it even begins.<br /><br />And of course Tyler's been busy. The grass roots Project Mayhem has globalize into Rize or Die (which is either a brilliant nod to the bro culture spawned by the movie, now commercialized and brought to you by Axe body spray, or just patently lazy)<br /><br />it's the same question I ask when Chuck Palahniuk appears in the comic wrestling with how to move the story forward. By the time he breaks the fourth wall and gives up any responsibility for a singular narrative ending I'm pretty invested in lazy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9616047210300923390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1706505472" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1706505472" />
    <a title="Andrew Edstrom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7701162-andrew-edstrom"><img alt="Andrew Edstrom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329980542p2/7701162.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1706505472?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andrew Edstrom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andrew Edstrom" href="/user/show/7701162-andrew-edstrom">Andrew Edstrom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1706505472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer127867174560193139">I mean Chuck Palahniuk knew fans would hate this book. He drew himself as a character in the book with an angry mob of fans holding nooses standing at his door. That doesn't make what he did okay, of course. But maybe it's part of, I don't know, some art thing he's trying to do? I'm trying to give him the benefit of the doubt here.<br/><br/>I feel like at the point where it was so clear to him that fans were going to hate this book that he was actually going to draw it as a scene within the book itself, h</span>
  <span id="freeText127867174560193139" style="display:none">I mean Chuck Palahniuk knew fans would hate this book. He drew himself as a character in the book with an angry mob of fans holding nooses standing at his door. That doesn't make what he did okay, of course. But maybe it's part of, I don't know, some art thing he's trying to do? I'm trying to give him the benefit of the doubt here.<br /><br />I feel like at the point where it was so clear to him that fans were going to hate this book that he was actually going to draw it as a scene within the book itself, he should have stopped and thought "Maybe I've hit a dead end here. Also maybe this is more meta than it is good. Maybe I should reconsider this whole Fight Club 2 business and let the original book continue standing on its own, as it's been doing just fine for the last 20 years. Maybe I should listen to the people in my writing group rather than just writing their objections into the story." <br /><br />Or maybe it's the best thing he's ever written and it just went completely over my head. I don't know. I'm kind of at a loss on this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="127867174560193139" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2385340591" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2385340591" />
    <a title="Michelle Curie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27203016-michelle-curie"><img alt="Michelle Curie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600963618p2/27203016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2385340591?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michelle Curie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michelle Curie" href="/user/show/27203016-michelle-curie">Michelle Curie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27203016-michelle-curie?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2385340591" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5796678620201663450"><b>
  <i>"I refuse to give readers an uplifting faux experience engineered to comfort them and perpetuate the sociopolitical and economic status quo."</i>
</b><br/><br/>Many stories are granted the status of <i>a classic</i> after a certain amount of time has passed - often decades, sometimes even centuries. Chuck Palahniuk was one of the authors who got to experience how his work started something close to a cultural movement. And how do you cope with a situation that no one has ever prepared you for? In many ways, that's th</span>
  <span id="freeText5796678620201663450" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>"I refuse to give readers an uplifting faux experience engineered to comfort them and perpetuate the sociopolitical and economic status quo."</i>
</b><br><br>Many stories are granted the status of <i>a classic</i> after a certain amount of time has passed - often decades, sometimes even centuries. Chuck Palahniuk was one of the authors who got to experience how his work started something close to a cultural movement. And how do you cope with a situation that no one has ever prepared you for? In many ways, that's the question <i>Fight Club 2</i> is seeking the answer to.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525764991i/25502256._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ten years have passed, the nameless narrator now calls himself Sebastian and he lives a mundane life with Marla and their son. He's now on medication, which help him with his insomnia and make Tylor stay away. But Marla misses that side of him, and when she starts to mess with his medication, Tylor finds a way to reemerge and trigger Armageddon. Or, as he and his space monkey call it: The Tranquility Gambit. <br><br>This sounds like a horribly bad idea of a story, and yes, it is. <i>Fight Club 2</i> is nothing but a disillusionment. It fails to be as impactful and hard-hitting as its predecessor, but it also never meant to be. Instead, Palahniuk uses this medium to reflect on what he has created, realizing that by writing the story of Tylor Durden, he started something that is now way more than the sum of its parts.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525764703i/25502252._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It all gets very <i>meta</i> and self-indulgent, which is funny, but also nothing I really needed. There's a scene in which Palahniuk is confronted with his fans, some of which didn't even know the film was based on a book, some of which are covered in tattoos with quotes, most of which are angry with Palahniuk's sequel or the way he is trying to write it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1525764703i/25502253._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So instead of really being a new story or a proper sequel, this is a rumination of what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2376722763" rel="nofollow noopener">Fight Club</a> has started. It's questionable whether his was really necessary and it feels like Palahniuk wrote it more for himself than for an audience. Fanboys might enjoy the meta-humor and the revival of some familiar quotes and moments, but all in all, I could have done easily without.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5796678620201663450" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8e2KfNeRk11b8IhPJHNPZGWlI3wNVb8KDyBlDLA/HRWvs3my1Xn/pgaUr9eB06jbOnh5OHyn+1BuuoIlHTSDzg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('N6dA9m4hUW2dM1/tT66ZtB/9JcMLYtKfOhnUWffdR1Np+bM4bMk9lsBXeHXqDn4LQCB/h3qQlsVbgzNwWtbZiA==')})
  }

Piètres débuts : quand le lecteur fait sa connaissance, il est torse nu, pas rasé, pieds et mains attachés à un radeau grossier, en train de dériver au gré des courants du Pacifique. Sa route a croisé celles de grandes figures de l\'Histoire. Il s\'est initié aux mystères de l\'ésotérisme, frotté aux secrets de la kabbale et de la franc-maçonnerie.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2546.Chuck_Palahniuk">About Chuck Palahniuk</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2546.Chuck_Palahniuk"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1391203076p3/2546.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<a href="/author/show/2546.Chuck_Palahniuk">Chuck Palahniuk

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6060832915905449279">Written in stolen moments under truck chassis and on park benches to a soundtrack of The Downward Spiral and Pablo Honey, <i>Fight Club</i> came into existence. The adaptation of <i>Fight Club</i> was a flop at the box office, but achieved cult status on DVD. The film’s popularity drove sales of the novel. Chuck put out two novels in 1999, <i>Survivor</i> and <i>Invisible Monsters</i>. <i>Choke</i>, published in 2001, became Chuck’</span>
  <span id="freeText6060832915905449279" style="display:none">Written in stolen moments under truck chassis and on park benches to a soundtrack of The Downward Spiral and Pablo Honey, <i>Fight Club</i> came into existence. The adaptation of <i>Fight Club</i> was a flop at the box office, but achieved cult status on DVD. The film’s popularity drove sales of the novel. Chuck put out two novels in 1999, <i>Survivor</i> and <i>Invisible Monsters</i>. <i>Choke</i>, published in 2001, became Chuck’s first New York Times bestseller. Chuck’s work has always been infused with personal experience, and his next novel, <i>Lullaby</i>, was no exception. Chuck credits writing <i>Lullaby</i> with helping him cope with the tragic death of his father. <i>Diary</i> and the non-fiction guide to Portland, <i>Fugitives and Refugees</i>, were released in 2003. While on the road in support of <i>Diary</i>, Chuck began reading a short story entitled 'Guts,' which would eventually become part of the novel <i>Haunted</i>.<br /><br />In the years that followed, he continued to write, publishing the bestselling <i>Rant, Snuff, Pygmy, Tell-All, a 'remix' of Invisible Monsters, Damned</i>, and most recently, <i>Doomed</i>. <br /><br />Chuck also enjoys giving back to his fans, and teaching the art of storytelling has been an important part of that. In 2004, Chuck began submitting essays to ChuckPalahniuk.net on the craft of writing. These were 'How To' pieces, straight out of Chuck's personal bag of tricks, based on the tenants of minimalism he learned from Tom Spanbauer. Every month, a “Homework Assignment” would accompany the lesson, so Workshop members could apply what they had learned. (all 36 of these essays can currently be found on The Cult's sister-site, LitReactor.com).<br /><br />Then, in 2009, Chuck increased his involvement by committing to read and review a selection of fan-written stories each month. The best stories are currently set to be published in <i>Burnt Tongues</i>, a forthcoming anthology, with an introduction written by Chuck himself. <br /><br />His next novel, <i>Beautiful You</i>, is due out in October 2014.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6060832915905449279" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
